Gu Xinyi Discusses the Freefall of Wheat Flour Prices and Relief Measures

How American Wheat is Sold

Is of Utmost Importance

At last week's Executive Yuan meeting, President Wang proposed an investigation into the state of wheat production to facilitate relief efforts. Currently, various ministries, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and the responsible bureaus of both Shanghai and Nanjing are diligently conducting this investigation. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency, recognizing the implications for farmers' economies and the government's determination to regulate wheat production, visited Mr. Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Mechanical Flour Milling Industry Association, as Shanghai is the hub for flour mills and a major center for wheat sales, making the matter of particular importance. The following is his account:

Wheat Production Statistics

According to him, there has historically been a lack of statistical data regarding domestic wheat production, leaving no basis for understanding the actual figures. This year's wheat harvest, encompassing the three provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, and Zhejiang, is estimated at approximately 15 million dan (a unit of dry measure, approximately 100 liters). Jiangsu has the largest yield, accounting for 75% of the total, while Anhui and Zhejiang together account for 35%. The current wheat reserves in Shanghai flour mills are approximately 3 million dan, primarily consisting of foreign wheat, estimated at about 2 million dan, with 1 million dan being domestic wheat. Market wheat reserves are also at 600,000 dan, predominantly domestic wheat, estimated at about 450,000 dan, with only 150,000 dan of foreign wheat. Recently, wheat arrivals have been averaging 40,000 to 50,000 dan daily, mostly Jiangbei wheat, with more going to Wuxi. In Wuxi, mills hold 300,000 dan and the market holds 400,000 dan, with daily arrivals of about 5,000 dan. This year's foreign wheat imports (from January to July) peaked in February and March, totaling about 7.5 million dan, primarily Australian wheat, accounting for about 80%. Wheat from America, Canada, and Argentina accounts for the remaining 20%. Wheat consumption in flour mills varies depending on their flour production capacity. Shanghai factories produce approximately 120,000 bags of flour daily, consuming about 60,000 dan of wheat. Assuming a 300-day operating year, annual wheat consumption is approximately 18 million dan. Factoring in both foreign and domestic wheat, this equates to 7.2 million dan of foreign wheat and 10.8 million dan of domestic wheat. Outside Shanghai, Wuxi has the most mills, producing about 300 bags of flour daily and consuming about 15,000 dan of wheat. Changzhou, Zhenjiang, and four other locations have a total of 9 mills, capable of producing 30,000 bags of flour daily and consuming about 15,000 dan of wheat. Therefore, the entire province of Jiangsu can produce 180,000 bags of flour daily, consuming about 90,000 dan of wheat. Attached table (in units of 1,000 bags/1,000 dan):

Address Number of Mills Daily Production Daily Consumption Mill Reserves Mill Reserves Market Reserves

of Flour of Wheat of Flour of Wheat of Wheat

Shanghai 15 120,000 60,000 3,000,000 3,000,000 600,000

Wuxi 3 12,000 15,000 300,000 300,000 400,000

Changzhou 1 3,000 1,500 Unknown Unknown Unknown

Zhenjiang 1 4,000 2,000 Unknown Unknown Unknown

Taizhou 1 3,000 1,500 Unknown Unknown Unknown

Qingjiangpu 1 2,000 1,000 Unknown Unknown Unknown

Haizhou 1 3,000 1,500 Unknown Unknown Unknown

Nanjing 4 15,000 7,500 Unknown Unknown Unknown

(Note) Flour is measured in units of 49 pounds per bag, and wheat is measured in units of 100 liters per dan. The numbers listed above are mostly estimates.

Of the 3 million bags of flour currently in storage in Shanghai, 2 million bags are grade 2 flour, 400,000 bags are grade 3 flour, and 600,000 bags are grade 4 flour.

The Course of Change

Wheat was priced at approximately five yuan per dan in the spring of this year. The standard price for new wheat at the February opening auction was also at four yuan sixty or seventy fen. However, by August, the price had fallen to a low of three yuan fifty-three fen. The price of rice was also two yuan seventy or eighty fen in the spring, dropping to two yuan forty or fifty fen when new wheat came onto the market, and further down to two yuan eighteen fen in August. The reasons for these changes and the decline in wheat prices are generally as stated in the recent special economic issue of Shen Bao, but the primary cause is the sluggish flour sales. Wheat's market is flour, and if flour is stockpiling unsold, wheat's outlet is cut off. Shanghai's own flour market has historically been mainly in the north, such as the areas around Beijing, Tianjin, and the three northeastern provinces, which were the largest sales areas for the mills. Since the Northeast fell, the market has been monopolized by Japanese flour mills, which have pushed out Shanghai's flour. Then Japanese flour invaded Beijing and Tianjin, followed by the Soviets, all backed by their respective national governments, dumping their flour regardless of cost. Chinese flour mills are generally operated by merchants with limited capital and cannot compete with the support of Japan and Russia. As a result, Shanghai flour mills' northern sales have dwindled, stocks have increased, and production has decreased, leading to a corresponding reduction in wheat consumption. Furthermore, the slump in rice prices has impacted grain prices, and the abundant harvests of various coarse grains have further affected the sales of machine-milled flour, as wheat-producing areas also have locally milled flour. Currently, Shanghai mills only sell slightly over 30,000 bags of flour to other cities, and about 20,000 bags are sold in Shanghai and its surrounding areas, totaling only half of the daily flour production. This has led to a large surplus of over 3 million bags. The future is uncertain, and unless prompt remedies are taken, the consequences will be unimaginable.

Relief Measures

Wheat is the raw material for flour, and increased flour sales will expand wheat demand. Therefore, rescuing flour is essentially rescuing wheat. The solutions to rescue flour are: (1) How to sell the American wheat that has been borrowed is a critical and difficult issue. However, it is imperative that (A) it absolutely not be sold to foreign merchants, as this would be like giving wings to a tiger and supplying food to the enemy. (B) The Cotton and Wheat Affairs Office should, in conjunction with the Flour Milling Industry Association and the Grain Association, develop a sound plan to distribute the American wheat to Chinese merchants of all sizes. (2) Import duties have already been imposed on imported flour, yet Japanese and Russian flour continue to flood the market, indicating dumping at prices below cost. The government should implement anti-dumping taxes as soon as possible. (3) Local officials are levying excessive taxes on wheat, which should be reduced or exempted to facilitate exports. (4) Farmers in wheat-producing areas need financial assistance to prevent them from rushing to sell, flooding the market with supply exceeding demand, driving down prices further, and causing even greater losses to farmers. It is hoped that the government authorities will promptly take steps to provide relief.

Turmoil at British American Tobacco Factory

Workers' Opinions Divided

Misunderstandings Arise Between Both Parties

The Disturbance is Temporarily Calmed

Da Gong News reports that the labor strike at the British American Tobacco Company's new and old factories in Pudong remains unresolved. Yesterday morning, over a thousand workers from the new factory's printing department secretly convened and advocated for resuming work. They also went to the union to demand answers, leading to serious disturbances. Upon hearing of this, the Public Security Bureau dispatched a large number of police officers to the scene to maintain order. Fortunately, no accidents occurred. The labor dispute issue has been scheduled for arbitration by the municipal government. Details are as follows:

Advocating for Returning to Work Over a thousand workers in the printing department of the British American Tobacco Company's Factory No. 2 in Lujiazui, Pudong, have traditionally enjoyed better treatment than workers in other departments. Since the declaration of a general strike in both new and old factories, there has been no hope for a resolution. Consequently, several workers, including Pan Quanrong from the printing department of the new factory, advocated for a decision to resume work unanimously, starting tomorrow (today). This sparked outrage among other workers, who viewed it as undermining unity. Representatives were sent to report to the union. Upon learning of this, the union immediately sent representatives to summon Pan Quanrong to the meeting for questioning. Given the large gathering of workers outside, the union, fearing accidents, advised Pan Quanrong to wait at the meeting, leading to misunderstandings among the workers in the printing department.

Gathering to Demand Answers Over a thousand workers from the printing department of the new factory misunderstood that Pan Quanrong was being detained by the union. They immediately gathered several hundred workers and went to the Fifth District Cigarette Workers' Union in Laiyidu to demand answers. Upon hearing of this, workers from other departments also misunderstood that the workers in the printing department were gathering to seize the union. They immediately gathered over a thousand people to protect the area around the union. For a time, the two groups of workers were facing off, creating a very dangerous situation.

Heads Confer The executive committee and supervisors of the Fifth District Cigarette Workers' Union, realizing the misunderstanding between the two groups of workers and fearing an incident, immediately summoned the heads of the printing department of the new factory to the meeting for questioning. The heads all stated that Pan Quanrong did indeed convene a secret meeting of workers in the printing department in an attempt to undermine the strike. At this time, dozens of workers outside the door suddenly sounded whistles, intending to rush into the union.

Police Dispatched to Maintain Order Zhang Mingqin, the district chief of the Third District Public Security Bureau, after receiving a report from the guard, personally led over twenty armed police officers to the scene to maintain order. However, due to the large number of people, it was difficult to disperse them immediately. He then telegraphed the Second Brigade of the Security Force for assistance. The brigade dispatched a squad of motorized bicycle police and a company of box cannon police to assist in maintaining order. A temporary lockdown was imposed until 4 PM, when the crowds gradually dispersed. Over twenty police officers from the Third District Public Security Bureau and the Security Force were stationed at the Fifth District Cigarette Workers' Union to provide protection and prevent further disturbances.

Seeking Instructions from the Party Committee The Fifth District Cigarette Workers' Union, due to the misunderstanding between the workers, found it more difficult to resolve the dispute. Over a dozen representatives, including the directors Gen Jingguan and Liu Dehua, went to the Municipal Party Committee to seek instructions. Committee member Wu Kaixian met with them, and after inquiring about the situation, dispatched Li Weixiong, a staff member of the Civil Affairs Section, to thoroughly investigate the truth before further action. He also notified the Third District Public Security Bureau to provide strict protection and prevent incidents.

Union Precautions The Fifth District Cigarette Workers' Union received reports that the printing department workers, after being dispersed by the police, returned to the factory to hold a secret meeting and planned to gather again today to demand answers. To prevent this, in addition to requesting police protection from the Public Security Bureau, the union organized a disciplinary team of 120 people, as well as propaganda teams, maintenance teams, and inspection teams, totaling over a thousand people, to maintain strict vigilance near the union starting last night.

Requesting Song's Mediation The New Voice News reports that the Fifth District Cigarette Workers' Union, after a strike in 1927 due to disputes over national taxes, was resolved through the mediation of Finance Minister Song Ziwen. In this situation, several attempts at mediation by the authorities have failed to produce results. Furthermore, the delegates' resolution to cope with the strike has worsened the situation. Now that the Minister of Finance has returned from the United States but has not yet returned to Nanjing, it is planned to send representatives to petition him in the coming days to take on the role of mediator.

Scheduled Arbitration After the union requested municipal government arbitration regarding British American Tobacco's failure to pay two days' wages due to the strike, the municipal government has scheduled arbitration for September 5th. Today, a notice was issued to both parties, stating, "Regarding the notification matter, the committee has scheduled September 5th (Tuesday) at 3 PM for arbitration in the case of the labor reduction dispute with the British American Tobacco Company. You are hereby ordered to send two representatives to the hearing to present your opinions and await arbitration. This notice is issued by Luo Pan, Chairman of the Shanghai Special Municipality Labor-Management Arbitration Committee, on August 29, 1933."

Soliciting Opinions The Municipal Government Secretariat, recognizing the worsening British American Tobacco dispute, issued an order to both parties yesterday to solicit opinions. The original order stated, "Regarding the order received that the Provisional Regulations for Factory Operations Management of the British American Tobacco Company should be amended urgently to eliminate disputes, the office may send letters to both labor and management to solicit opinions, compile them, and submit them for handling." In addition to sending separate letters, this letter is sent for your information. Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Government Secretariat, August 28, 1933.

A Returning Traveler from Xinjiang Speaks

Luo Liqing Discusses the Recent Situation in Xinjiang Province

Xinjiang borders Russia, is vast and sparsely populated, and has extremely rich reserves of forests and minerals. The Chinese people do not know how to develop them, allowing foreigners to covet them. Since Yang Zengxin, the rulers have embraced a policy of isolationism, causing news to be cut off from the interior. Very few Chinese people know the state of Xinjiang. Recently, after Jin Shuren fled, the central government appointed Huang Musong to go to Xinjiang to comfort and investigate. Unexpectedly, after arriving in Xinjiang, Sheng Shicai suddenly shot and killed the backbone members of the new faction, such as Tao Mingyue, which caused a second coup. The content is complex, and outsiders know very little. Mr. Luo Liqing, a counselor of the Envoy of Comfort Office, ventured to Xinjiang, endured hardships along the way, and finally returned to Shanghai yesterday after three months. The reporter visited Mr. Luo at the hotel and asked about recent events in Xinjiang. He replied in detail, which is recorded separately below.

Hardships on the Journey

Mr. Luo Liqing went to Xinjiang via Vladivostok, then the Siberian Railway, passing through Novosibirsk and Leningrad, before heading to Tacheng. The journey required sea travel, trains, and automobiles, and was fraught with hardship. Weitangzi is the border between China and Russia entering Xinjiang. From Baktu to Xinjiang Province, ordinary people must undergo strict inspections to get there, as both the Chinese and Russian sides have inspectors stationed there. As a central government official, Mr. Luo was exempt from inspection. Upon arriving in Tacheng, he was welcomed into the province by the local officials.

The Cause of the New Changes

The cause of the new changes was Jin Shuren's excessive oppression of the Hui and Kazakh ethnic groups, which led to riots. Sheng Shicai took the opportunity to rise up and drive out Jin, becoming the governor himself, with Liu Wenlong as the chairman of the province. Sheng was originally a subordinate of Guo Songling. In 1928, he was appointed as a colonel staff officer by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and got to know Lu Xiaozu, who brought him to Xinjiang. Yang Zengxin appointed him to a military position. He has only been in Xinjiang for three or four years. Liu Wenlong is a native of Zhejiang. His father had been an official in Xinjiang for a long time and was the original provincial committee member and director of the Education Department. He took advantage of the Hui rebellion to expel Jin and took on the dual roles of military and civilian leader of Xinjiang.

The Rise of the New Faction

When Jin Shuren fled, the backbone members of the new faction in Xinjiang formed a Provincial Government Maintenance Committee, including young people such as Chen Zhong (a Whampoa Military Academy student), Tao Mingyue (a provincial committee member), and Li Xiaotian. They opposed Sheng Shicai's rule and advocated for construction along the lines of Soviet Russia and a thorough reform of provincial administration. On June 11th, Huang Musong arrived in Xinjiang. Sheng had already led his troops to Guchengzi to attack Ma Zhongying. While Sheng was at the front, he heard that the young faction, including Chen and Li, were planning to reform the administration. So, after repelling Ma's army, on June 20th, he hurriedly returned to Dihua, the provincial capital, to deal with this matter.

Killing the Opposition

Upon returning to Dihua, Sheng immediately convened a provincial military and political conference and announced on the spot that three members of the opposition party must be shot. Tao Mingyue argued fiercely with Sheng at the conference and was immediately bound and paraded through the streets. The three men were executed together. At the same time, Huang Musong was placed under house arrest. The second coup then began. That evening, Sheng also arrested and killed eight people who were affiliated with the young faction. The charges were not announced. Huang Musong was detained from June 21st to July 18th, when he was released and returned to Nanjing after being summoned by the central government. This ended the second coup.

The Xinjiang Army

The Xinjiang Provincial Army, commanded by the First Division under Li Hairu, has approximately 6,000 soldiers and is well-equipped with guns and cannons. A brigade in Qitai has already surrendered to Ma Zhongying. There is an artillery battalion in Tacheng, commanded by Battalion Commander Xian Anbang, with approximately 300 soldiers. Sheng Shicai's troops include over 2,000 miscellaneous soldiers from the northern route, as well as 1,500 White Russian naturalized soldiers, known for their fighting prowess, who are directly under Sheng's command. There is a division in Yili under Zhang Peiyuan, which has recently incorporated the remnants of Jin Shuren's troops, with a strength of approximately 7,000 men. There are also soldiers who retreated into Xinjiang from the Anti-Japanese Railway Protection Army, including Zheng Ziliang's brigade under Su Bingwen, which has now been replenished to approximately 5,000 men, mostly stationed in Dihua.

The rest are Su's guard battalion, commanded by Battalion Commander Wang Qingyun, with over 300 soldiers stationed in Tacheng. In addition, there are approximately 4,000 men who retreated into Xinjiang from the troops of Li Du, Ding Chao, and Wang Delin, but there are more than ten brigade commanders.

Russian Influence

Russia borders Xinjiang. In recent years, the Soviet Union has been gradually carrying out economic aggression against Xinjiang. Since Jin Shuren signed a secret agreement with Soviet Russia and signed contracts for the purchase of aircraft, military equipment, and automobiles, he secretly allowed Russians to freely enter the interior of Xinjiang to buy, sell, and trade. He also allowed Russians to establish a financial bureau in Xinjiang. Currently, the economic power of Xinjiang is almost entirely in the hands of the Russians. There are already more than 50,000 White Russians who have been naturalized and reside in Xinjiang, engaged in agriculture and commerce.

The Current Situation of the People

The ethnic groups in Xinjiang are divided into Han, Manchu, Hui, Uyghur, and Kazakh, resulting in diverse races. They have been oppressed by the authorities over the years, and riots have often occurred. According to Mr. Luo, the Hui, Kazakh, Uyghur, and other ethnic groups are actually very enthusiastic about obeying our central government. If the rulers can guide them according to the situation and not discriminate against them, they can live in peace. During Luo's trip to Tacheng, all the Hui people expressed their sincere welcome. Mr. Luo also proclaimed the virtues of the central government, and the people were overjoyed. At that time, Kazakh chiefs such as Issak and Timur Baike held meetings to welcome him and gathered people's groups to hold dance parties, which shows their sincerity.

A Glimpse of the Economy

Most of the people in Xinjiang are wealthy and save gold bars and silver coins. The rich have five hundred taels, and the poor have fifty taels. Some people cultivate paddy fields, while others are nomadic. As for the money in circulation, the Provincial Department of Finance issues a silver tael paper currency. Each tael of paper currency is worth half a yuan in national currency. Recently, due to excessive issuance, the market is flooded with paper silver, totaling as much as 200 million, causing the value of the currency to fall daily. Each national currency can buy more than forty taels of paper silver. As a result, there is less and less silver in the hands of the people, and prices are gradually becoming more expensive. Xinjiang produces the world-renowned Turpan cotton, as well as valuable furs, forests, petroleum, crystal rock salt, gold, silver, jewels, jade, and deer antlers.

Sightseeing in Kulun

After arriving in Xinjiang, Mr. Luo also visited Kulun and exchanged greetings with the Mongolian New Government authorities. In his capacity as a private citizen, Mr. Luo flew to Kulun and stayed for about ten hours, receiving a warm welcome from the New Government authorities. Mongolian New Government officials, including Prince Yi Li Bo of the Right Wing, Duke Ai Lin of the Supporting State, Sida Bija, the head of the Altai Kazakh people, and the chief of the twelve Keliyi households, all welcomed him at the station, hosted him at a banquet inside the New Government, and led him to visit the Lama Temple. Mr. Luo was urgently recalled by a telegram from the central government, so he could not stay long and left Kulun to return to China.

Ma's Army Rebellion

When the reporter asked about Ma Zhongying's recent situation, Mr. Luo replied that since he left Dihua on the 10th of this month, he often heard the sound of Ma attacking the provincial capital. Ma currently has tens of thousands of troops, and even more followers from the Hui rebellion. Ma's troops are located in the Yanqi area southwest of the Tianshan Mountains. Dihua is reportedly launching an encirclement attack, and Sheng Shicai is mobilizing troops to meet him. I was on the way in the past three weeks, so the truth is unclear.

Seeking Shandong People in Xinjiang

There are many people from Shandong Province who do business and farm in Xinjiang. These Shandong people were originally in Soviet Russia. Recently, due to the signing of treaties by Russia, they cannot return to China from Vladivostok, so many have changed their route and returned from Xinjiang. After arriving in Xinjiang, they stayed there. There are currently no fewer than 50,000 Shandong people in the province. The Russian compatriots in Soviet Russia go to Xinjiang and are issued passports by Consul Mo stationed in Tacheng. Each batch involves three to four thousand people.

Land Bureau Announces that Property Owners Must Report Land Prices Themselves

Begins Tomorrow and Lasts Until the End of September

Landowners in Shanghai South and Zhabei Districts Must Report First

The Shanghai Land Bureau, in order to collect land value tax, issued Announcement No. 69 yesterday, based on the provision in Article 6 of the Provisional Regulations that property owners must report land prices themselves. The announcement stipulates that from September 1st to the end of the month, property owners must come to the bureau to obtain forms and report their land prices. The original text is recorded below: "Regarding the announcement, all chapters, detailed rules, and land value tax zoning maps for the collection of the provisional land value tax in this city have been announced successively, and the collection has been set to begin on August 1st of this year. Based on Article 6 of the Shanghai Provisional Land Value Tax Collection Regulations and Articles 3 and 4 of the Implementing Detailed Rules of the same regulations, the deadline for property owners to report land prices is set from September 1st to September 30th of this year. All property owners in the Shanghai South and Zhabei districts that have been included in the collection area must come to the bureau to obtain land price reporting forms within the deadline. No extensions will be granted after the deadline. Other districts should wait for subsequent announcements. This matter is important. Obey accordingly. This announcement is issued by Jin Liren, Director of the Bureau."

Zhang Yuanfu Arrives in Shanghai from Nanjing

Nanjing, August 30th (Central News Agency) - Zhang Yuanfu, the representative of Sheng Shicai, the Border Defense Commissioner of Xinjiang, arrived in Nanjing yesterday on a Eurasian Airlines flight from Xinjiang. He had a discussion with Zhang Fengjiu, the representative of Xinjiang Province stationed in Nanjing. On the morning of the 30th, he traveled to Shanghai from Nanjing by train. He will return to Nanjing in a few days to report on the recent situation in Xinjiang Province to President Wang, and then go to Guling to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. It is rumored that Mr. Zhang brought some red gold to Shanghai to convert it into cash.

The Queen of the Netherlands' Birthday Today

The Dutch Consulate General Holds a Celebration

Today is the 53rd birthday of the Queen of the Netherlands. The Dutch Consulate General in this city is holding a celebration as usual. A celebration ceremony will be held at the consulate today, and foreign guests will be invited. Mayor Wu Tiecheng of the Municipal Government, as well as Yu Ming, Director of the Foreign Affairs Office, and Zhao Tiezhang, Chief of the Section, will all go to offer congratulations today to strengthen friendly relations.

Jiangsu Provincial Government Allocates Funds to Repair the Seawall

Reply to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Local Collaboration Association previously sent a joint telegram to the Jiangsu Provincial Government regarding the dangerous situation of the Baoshan seawall, requesting that funds for labor and materials be prepared in advance to expedite repairs. The provincial government has now replied, stating, "Your telegram has been received. Two million yuan has already been allocated for the emergency repair project of the seawall in the county, and the county magistrate has been ordered to start construction immediately. The breach of the Yellow River in the counties of Lanfeng, Changheng, Dongming, etc., is serious. Jiangsu is located downstream and is particularly concerned about the disaster. It has repeatedly telegraphed the central government to dispatch senior officials to preside over the blocking and restoration, and has also telegraphed the counties along the canal to take protective measures. Recently, it has been reported that the breach in Lanfeng is no longer flooding, and the Dongming water is flowing into southern Shandong, reaching the Weishan Lake, and there is a trend of flowing into the central canal. Please inform accordingly. This reply."

Ministry of Finance Rejects Chamber of Commerce's Request to Issue Transportation Certificates for Stored Tobacco

Local Tobacco Leaves with Old Taxes Paid

Are Exempt from Special Tax in This City

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Tobacco Leaf Industry Association regarding the problems that may arise in the transportation of stored tobacco after the special tax on local tobacco leaves was introduced. It requested that the Ministry of Finance be telegraphed to issue certificates for the transportation of old tobacco when local tobacco leaves with old taxes paid are transported to other cities to exempt them from paying the new tax. After the telegram was sent, the Ministry of Finance replied, stating, "Your telegram has been received. Regarding the collection of the special tax on local tobacco leaves, the measures for paying the new tax and refunding the old tax on inventory issued by the Taxation Department stipulate that local tobacco leaves stored in this city that have paid the old tax should be reported and converted to the special tax before July 31st before being allowed to be sold and transported. Subsequently, the Shanghai Tobacco Leaf Industry Association stated the difficulties, and the department, in order to accommodate the merchants, revised the original measures and separately reviewed and supplemented various points. It allowed local tobacco leaves that had paid the old tax before July and were stored in Shanghai to be sold in this city within a period of three months, i.e., from July to the end of September, without being required to pay the special tax. However, within three months, if local tobacco leaves are transported from Shanghai to other cities, the old tax should still be refunded at any time, and the special tax should be reported and paid before they are allowed to be exported, to show a compromise. The association was notified separately and the Jiangsu Stamp Tax and Tobacco and Alcohol Bureau was ordered to comply. The merchants should understand and comply, and there is no need to make further requests. The request to issue transportation certificates for stored tobacco transported to other cities to exempt them from the new tax should not be considered. In addition to informing the Jiangsu Stamp Tax and Tobacco and Alcohol Bureau, this reply is hereby issued. Inform accordingly. This reply."

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Sends Personnel to Fiji to Investigate Sanitary Administration

Yi Wenzhi and Wu Deming Set Off Yesterday

Trade between China and Fiji is developing rapidly. This spring, the Fijian government organized a delegation to visit China. In April, they sent Minister of Health, Dr. Forkardt, to China to investigate the health situation in our country and to investigate the manufacturing methods of our exported ham and meat products. They are deeply concerned about trade between China and Fiji. Cai Wuji, Director of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, believes that the bureau's responsibility is to manage inspections and assist merchants in developing foreign trade. A large quantity of our country's meat and ham is sold to Fiji. However, because the island is not clear about our manufacturing methods, it often uses the excuse of non-compliance with hygiene standards to prohibit imports, which has a great impact on our country's trade with Fiji. The island's sanitation facilities are known to be perfect, and it pays special attention to the inspection of imported food. It is urgent to send personnel to promote and investigate separately, so as to facilitate sales and provide a reference for our country. Therefore, the bureau has specially dispatched Fijian technical officer Yi Wenzhi and technician Wu Deming to Fiji to investigate everything. They set off yesterday (the 30th) and have reported to Minister Chen of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for review and record.

Ministry of Railways Orders Railway Bureau to Investigate Wheat Sales Stagnation

Specifies Scope and Methods of Investigation

Railway Bureau Has Ordered the Transportation Department to Comply

The Railway Bureau received a telegram from Minister of Railways Gu Mengyu yesterday, ordering an investigation into the stagnation of wheat sales along the railway lines. After receiving the telegram, the bureau has ordered the Transportation Department to comply. The original telegram is recorded on the left:

Scope of Investigation

Kyoto-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus, please note: We have now received instructions from President Wang, ordering a prompt investigation into the stagnation of wheat sales in various places. Therefore, we telegraph to each railway, quickly select major stations adjacent to famous wheat-producing or selling areas along each railway, and immediately order each station to quickly determine the situation of wheat in various places regarding the following items, by contacting the Grain Associations or other relevant organizations in the cities near each station. Each station should telegraph directly to the Business Department of the Ministry.

Prescribed Methods

Details are as follows: (A) Names of important wheat-producing areas near the station; (B) How was the harvest in each producing area last year and this year; (C) How many dan (a unit of dry measure) of wheat were produced in each producing area this year; (D) How many dan of wheat are currently stockpiled in each producing area and available for distribution; (E) From August 1st to 23rd of this year, what were the highest, lowest, and average wholesale market prices per dan in each producing area, and how does this compare to the market prices during the same period in ordinary years; (F) How many dan of wheat were shipped out by railway by the station and are currently stockpiled awaiting shipment; (G) Names of important wheat-selling areas near the station; (H) Whether there is any stockpiled wheat in each selling area, and how many dan; (I) During the above-mentioned period, what were the highest, lowest, and average wholesale market prices per dan in each selling area, and how does this compare to the market prices during the same period in ordinary years; (J) How many dan of wheat were shipped in by railway by the station and are currently stockpiled.

Deadline for Telegram Reply

When replying by telegram, the above items should be replaced with A, B, C, D, etc. as much as possible. Also, the quantity should be in dan, and the price per dan should be in silver dollars. The number of kilograms per dan locally must be clearly stated. Furthermore, two or three capable staff members with economic knowledge should be dispatched by the railway to supervise and ensure accurate handling. The reply telegram must be sent within five days of receiving the telegram, without delay. Furthermore, the investigation of the quantity, price, etc. of wheat in various places should continue according to the above-mentioned methods, but the period of investigation should be changed to one week. The situation each week, except for items A, F, C, and G, which do not need to be re-reported, the remaining items should still be telegraphed by the station every Monday. Please comply and follow accordingly, this is of utmost importance.

Telegram Received by Anhui Fellow Provincial Association

Han Shan County Besieged by Bandits

The Anhui Fellow Provincial Association recently received a telegram from a large merchant in He County, stating that at 6:00 AM on the 26th of this month, a large group of ferocious bandits entered Han Shan County, committing arson, murder, rape, and plunder in a cruel manner. The local authorities did not fire a single shot to resist. The bandits occupied the county town for two days and nights, looting until 8:00 AM on the 28th, before retreating to a mountain recess on the outskirts. They are still gathering and have not dispersed. If they are not severely suppressed, it is feared that the tragedy of Fuyang and Yingzhou will happen again near the capital.

Traces of Prominent Figures

Sun Ke, Ma Chaojun, Fu Rulin, Fu Bingchang, and Liu Ruiheng took the night express train to Beijing last night.

Xu Shiying and Li Shijia left Beijing by train last night and arrived in Shanghai this morning.

Change of Head of Dongsha Island Meteorological Station

The Dongsha Island Observatory of the Ministry of the Navy is responsible for the navigation marks and route guidance in the area. Although the place is a barren island with no inhabitants, it is important for shipping traffic. Therefore, the Ministry of the Navy sends a director and wireless operators to reside on the island every year to manage meteorological affairs. The term of office is two years, after which they are transferred. The current director of the station, Mr. Gu Houmo, has been ordered by the Ministry of the Navy to be transferred to the position of Major Staff Officer of the Coast Guard Department. The vacant position of station director will be filled by Mr. Shen Youqi, who has been appointed by the Ministry of the Navy. After receiving the order, Lieutenant Colonel Shen purchased a large amount of food and sundries the day before yesterday and set off for the island to take up his new post.

Anti-Japanese General Ends Up Polishing Shoes in Shanghai

Earning Over 30 Yuan a Month

Does Not Forget to Donate to Northeast Refugees

Jiang Minsheng, a former major general and advisor of Ding Chao's anti-Japanese army in Northeast China, a native of Harbin, has drifted to Shanghai. He has been given food and lodging by the Shanghai Charity Organizations and the Joint Relief Association for Northeast Refugees on Yunnan Road, which ensured his safety. Later, he was given some capital by the association to buy shoe polish and powder and started polishing shoes for pedestrians at the entrance of a lane next to the Cathay Theatre on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, which is enough for him to live on. Apart from expenses and savings, he specially donated funds to the association yesterday and sent it by letter to be remitted to the Northeast to relieve the refugees. The original letter reads, "Respectfully, Minsheng is drifting at sea and is honored to have been given food and lodging by your association. I am also grateful for your help in starting a small business to make a living. I started polishing shoes on July 25th and it has been a month now. The total income is 32.20 silver dollars. I respectfully donate 5 silver dollars to your association to save our Northeast refugees. The remaining amount is 10 yuan for postal savings, 4.50 yuan for buying shoe polish and boot powder, 6.20 yuan for pocket money, and 2.50 silver dollars for buying clothes. I still have 4 yuan in hand. I hereby report and express my gratitude. Respectfully presented to the Joint Relief Association for Northeast Refugees of Various Shanghai Charity Organizations."

The Trunk Murder Case Has Been Investigated

Victim Was Chopped to Death Before Being Dismembered

Court Orders Strict Arrest of the Murderer

Early in the morning the other day, a wooden trunk and a package were found at the entrance of the Cantonese People's Hospital at the intersection of Route D'Orleans and Paoan Road in Hongkou. After being opened and inspected, it was found that they contained a dismembered male corpse, a total of eight pieces. The detectives took them to the Route D'Orleans Police Station and photographed each piece of the head and limbs before taking them to the Forensic Examination Office on Rue Frelupt to await the official examination. Details have been reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, Prosecutor of the First Special District District Court, led forensic doctors Wei Ligong and Zhang Yan, and Clerk Wang Zuyi in a car to the office. Under the lawful examination of the two forensic doctors, they reported to the prosecutor that the examination revealed that the deceased was chopped in the vital parts of the head and chest with an ax-like weapon, causing death, and then the body was dismembered. Subsequently, the police station summoned Chen Zongming, a shop assistant at the Cantonese People's Hospital, for questioning. According to his statement, a patient in the hospital, Li Jiansheng, said that at that time, Li opened the window of the ward and looked out, and suddenly saw a rickshaw puller running with a car. In addition to a passenger, there was also a box and bedding on the car. When they arrived in front of the hospital, the car stopped, and the passenger moved the box and bedding to the ground. After the rickshaw puller left, the passenger also left. At first, he did not expect that the box and bedding contained a dismembered corpse. That is what Li said, and I don't know anything else. Since the dismemberment of the corpse has been verified, Prosecutor Guo ordered that it be handed over to the Pushan Mountain Villa for collection and burial, and ordered the police station to strictly arrest the murderer and bring him to justice. At the same time, in order to solve the case quickly, the police station specially announced a reward yesterday for the rickshaw puller who was hired at the time to go to the police station to report, and a bonus will be given to him.

Female Passenger on the Da Yu Steamer Commits Suicide by Jumping into the Sea

A Man and a Woman Boarded the Ship at Tianshenggang

The Man Has Now Been Sent to the Bureau by the Water Patrol Team

The Da Yu steamer of the Nanshi Dada Company, on its voyage back to Shanghai, had a young man and woman on board when it arrived at Tianshenggang midway. Unexpectedly, at about 6:00 AM yesterday morning, just as the ship was passing Yaogang and arriving at the Qiwangsha River, one of the two women suddenly jumped into the river and committed suicide. Although the ship stopped and attempted a rescue, it failed to retrieve the body. A man who traveled with her has been sent by the Water Patrol Corps of the Municipal Public Security Bureau to the Public Security Bureau for verification. The situation is very peculiar, and the details are described below.

Young Man and Woman Board the Ship Together

The Da Yu steamer of the Nanshi Dada Company set anchor from Tianshenggang at about 4:00 AM yesterday morning and set sail for Shanghai. At that time, two young men and women suddenly boarded the ship together at the Tianshenggang wharf, with three pieces of luggage and a small rattan basket. Because all the cabins were full, two berths were set up in the large kitchen room. Soon after the ship left the shore, the two men and women often went to the railings outside the large kitchen room to talk intimately.

After Passing Yaogang, the Woman Suddenly Jumps into the River

At about 6:00 AM, the ship passed Yaogang and arrived at the Qiwangsha River. The man suddenly walked into the large kitchen room and fell asleep on a military bed. Unexpectedly, the woman took this opportunity to jump into the river. Other passengers caught sight of it and were greatly shocked, causing an immediate commotion. The shipowner heard about it and quickly stopped the ship and tried to salvage the body, but the woman had disappeared without a trace.

The Man Who Came with Her Was Sent to the Water Patrol Team

Since the woman's suicide by jumping into the river was very closely related to the man, he was placed under surveillance. When the ship arrived in Shanghai at about 11:00 AM at noon, Dada Company prepared a letter and sent the man, together with the tea boy Chen Xiang who witnessed all the actions of the two men and women on the ship, and his luggage to the Water Patrol Team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requesting a thorough investigation. When Chief Zhu of the team conducted a preliminary trial of the case, the tea boy Chen Xiang on the ship confessed the previous situation and requested an investigation.

The Man Claims They Met by Chance

When questioned, the man claimed his name was Mao Mengjue, 22 years old, from Pingjiang, Hunan. Yesterday, I took a boat from Yongzhou to Tianshenggang and stayed at the Zhang Shunji Inn there in order to wait for a boat to Shanghai to find a job. Because the woman who jumped into the river also stayed at the inn, we got to know each other. After talking, she said that her surname was Zhang and that she had been studying at the Shanghai Wuben Girls' School. This time, because the school's opening date was near, she was waiting for a boat here to set off. At that time, I saw that her dress was very similar to that of a student, but she had a frowning expression, as if she had an unspeakable secret. However, I did not go into details because we met by chance.

Various Oppressions Led to an Early Suicide Plan

Then the woman suddenly wrote a note and sent it to me. The note stated that because of family economic and other pressures, she planned to commit suicide. However, she still lacked travel expenses for her studies in Shanghai, so she asked to borrow 3 silver dollars as travel expenses. After arriving in Shanghai, she would return the money immediately and would never break her promise. However, because I did not bring much travel expenses myself, I refused. However, I agreed to bear the cost of boat tickets and other expenses along the way to Shanghai. The woman also agreed. Later, we boarded the Da Yu steamer together.

The Matter Concerns Human Life, Sent to the Bureau for Verification

On the ship, the woman repeatedly revealed her intention to commit suicide. When I asked her the reason for her suicide, she refused to tell the truth. At that time, I tried my best to comfort her. Unexpectedly, at about 6:00 AM this morning, when the ship arrived at the Qiwangsha River, the woman took the opportunity of my sleeping soundly and jumped into the river. Because there are many untruths in the man's confession, an official document was prepared and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Eight More Guard Posts Added to the Extra-Territorial Road Construction in Western Shanghai

Scheduled to Be Established on September 1st

Since the winter of the 13th year of the Republic of China, during the Qi-Lu War, the British Public Works Department opened more than 20 roads outside the boundaries in the Fahua and Pusong areas of western Shanghai. Various French groups in Shanghai opposed this because it was a loss of sovereignty, and petitioned the National Government to protest strongly to the British Consulate. After repeated discussions between the two sides, the unconditional recovery has not been resolved, so that all administrative matters on the road are handled by the Public Works Department, which is an act of usurping power and humiliating the country. In view of this, the Municipal Government ordered the Municipal Public Security Bureau to add eight guard posts in the jurisdiction of the first and second sub-bureaus of the sixth district, namely, Qiaodun Road, Anhe Temple Road, and Daxi Road (the second sub-bureau of the sixth district), Lincoln Road, Robegen Road, MacArthur Road, Memorial Arch Road, and Pias Road (the first sub-bureau of the sixth district). Two classes of capable police officers will be selected for each post to take turns to be stationed there, as a precursor to the future recovery of the extra-territorial road construction. After receiving the order, Chief Liu Lun and Chief Bi Zhenhua immediately started work and spared no effort. The preparations have now been completed and the establishment is scheduled for September 1st.

Two Prisoners Preach Communism in Prison

And Copied Out Draft Documents for Preaching Communism

No Audience Allowed at the Trial; Sentencing Today

The young man Wu Liwen, 21 years old this year, was arrested by the political department of the French police for preaching communism in the French Concession and sent to the Third Branch Court of Jiangsu Higher Court for interrogation, where he was sentenced to imprisonment. Fu Heqing was arrested by the police in the French Concession for committing arson and sent to the Second Special District Court, where he was sentenced to imprisonment. Both were sent to the Second Special District Prison for execution. Unexpectedly, Wu still did not repent and colluded with Fu Heqing in prison to preach communism to the prisoners. Last month, when Wu and others were preaching to prisoners Yu Xishan, who was guilty of theft, and Wu Xuande, who was guilty of rebellion, they were seen by guard Song Cha. Documents for preaching communism were copied out from Wu's and Fu's sides and reported to the chief warden, who reported it to Warden Sun Xiongli, who detained Wu and Fu in another prison and prepared a document to transfer Wu and others to the Third Branch Court of Jiangsu Higher Court for interrogation. After repeated court investigations by Prosecutor Zhang Zongru of the High Court, a public prosecution was filed with the criminal court of the same level. Yesterday, Criminal Judge Zhou Yunhui, accompanied by Assessors Fan Peien and Li Shouyi, together with Prosecutor Zhang, convened the two prisoners Wu and Fu, the two prisoner witnesses Yu and Lu, and the guards to the third court for trial. Wu Liwen appointed lawyer Huang Zengjie as his defender. Fu Heqing was assigned lawyer Tu Kunfan by the court to defend him. Because Tu did not arrive, lawyer Huang was temporarily assigned to defend him. Because the case was political, no audience was allowed. It was heard that as a result of the trial, the court announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the 31st.

Young Man Commits Suicide by Jumping into the Huangpu River

At about 9:00 PM the night before last, a young man at the Xinkuang Wharf on Hankou Road suddenly jumped into the Huangpu River and committed suicide while people were not paying attention. At that time, a companion was standing on the dock enjoying the cool air. When he discovered it, he called out to the nearby boatmen to help him salvage the body, but the man's body sank and did not come up for a long time, so he could not be saved and drowned at the bottom of the river. At that time, a patrolman from the Customs Water Patrol Police Station arrived and took the deceased's companion to the police station. According to the statement, the deceased's name was Mei Chongxi, 20 years old, from Hubei. We both came to the dock together to enjoy the cool air. I don't know what the deceased had in mind, but he took the opportunity to commit suicide. As for what he was wearing, it was a white silk gauze long gown and white cloth trousers. The police chief ordered to notify the family of the deceased to send someone to salvage the body and collect it for burial.

Breaking Two Extortion Cases by Catching an Extortion Gang

Architect Li Zuxian Extorted 5,000 Yuan

Money Giant Qin Runqing Receives Two Threatening Letters

Li Zuxian, a Ningbo architect residing at No. 599 Jiaozhou Road, suddenly received a letter by mail at about 11:00 AM on the 13th of this month. Upon opening it, it was a threatening letter. The signatory was the Youth Anti-Traitor Group, and the language was fierce, demanding 5,000 yuan, saying that if he did not agree, they would use appropriate means to deal with him and arranged to contact him at the intersection of Xinzha Road and Wenzhou Road on the 16th. Li reported the letter to the Gordon Road Police Station in charge. The police chief ordered Chinese and foreign detectives to go to wait and see, but the bandits did not come. Unexpectedly, at 9:00 AM on the 18th, Li received another threatening letter, saying why he had sent police officers to wait last time, and now he specially warned him not to pay. He arranged to contact him at the intersection of Pike Road and Datong Road at 2:00 PM on the 19th. The person who came must put the paper money in a red paper bag. Li reported to the police station again and sent Chinese Detective Zhu Hanbo, Detective Liu Chunshu, and Pi Shaochang to hide nearby. On the one hand, Li's coachman, Li Ada, pretended to be a representative, carrying a red paper bag in the shape of 5,000 yuan of banknotes, and waited at the appointed place. At 4:10 PM, the bandit Lu Zhiquan, from Anhui, came, first wandering around Li Ada, intending to observe whether there were any undercover detectives. Then he stepped forward to talk to Li, took the red paper bag, and gave Li a receipt, carrying the bag and fleeing. He was chased and caught by the undercover detectives, and another receipt was copied out, which stated that Qin Runqing had received 5,000 yuan of ocean. He was taken to the police station for detention, and the next morning, he was sent to the First Special Court. After a questioning, because the police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that a receipt to Qin Runqing had been copied from the defendant, the defendant was still committing another case and requested a postponement. The court approved, and because the police station was investigating the case, the release was temporarily postponed. The Chinese and foreign detectives who handled the case investigated and found that Lu had written threatening letters twice on the 13th and 18th of this month, attempting to defraud the money tycoon Qin Runqing of 5,000 yuan. Because Qin did not report to the police station, he went to the Yuyuan Money Shop on Ningbo Road to retrieve the two threatening letters and took them back to the police station. Yesterday morning, the continued hearing was due. First, police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated the circumstances of the case, saying that the defendant was now prosecuted for attempted extortion under Article 370, Section 3 of the Criminal Law, and the police station had ordered the defendant to write a note. Under the comparison of the handwriting on the threatening letter and the receipt he sent, they were exactly the same. Therefore, the case was actually committed by the defendant and there was no doubt. The interrogation should be requested. Then, Qin Luoping, the son of Qin Runqing, claimed that my father went to Ningbo because of the death of a friend, but I did not know about this case at first. Until the police detectives came and said that my father had received a threatening letter, I went to the Yuyuan Money Shop. Because my father was not in Shanghai, all the letters were not opened and placed in the letter slot. Now that there was a threatening situation, I opened each letter and found two threatening letters inside, which were taken away by the detectives. When questioned, the defendant Lu Zhiquan confessed that the matter was initiated by Wang Jinkui, who was at large. I was really fooled by him. He shed tears as he spoke, with great remorse. After Judge Xue verified the confession, he ordered that the interrogation of the case be concluded and the sentencing be postponed to September 6. The defendant was returned to the police station.

Zhang Shizhao and Others File an Appeal for the Liu Chongwu Case

丨Already Submitted to the Supreme Court丨

The patriotic youth Liu Chongwu and others, for throwing a bomb to warn treacherous merchants, were prosecuted by the police for premeditated murder. After a ruling by the appellate court, they were sentenced to twelve years in prison, causing dissatisfaction among various groups. An "Aid the Patriotic Volunteers Association" was organized, and a resolution was passed in a meeting to file an appeal. Chen Jiufeng was publicly elected to proceed with the matter, and three lawyers, Zhang Shizhao, Ma Junshuo, and Zou Shengzu, were hired to appeal to the Supreme Court. The appeal petition is recorded below:

Regarding the matter of supplementing the appeal, the Shanghai Public Concession Bureau prosecuted the defendants for premeditated murder. Judgment Document No. 14 of the 22nd Year of the Supreme Court stated: "The original judgment regarding Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, and Tian Shuiyang is revoked. Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, and Cao Songshou are each sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment for continuous joint premeditated murder. Tian Shuiyang is sentenced to six years of imprisonment for assisting in premeditated murder. The number of days detained before the judgment is final shall be offset against the imprisonment at the rate of two days for one day," etc. An appeal has been declared within the legal time limit. The legal reasons for disagreeing with the original judgment are presented in detail as follows: The original judgment revoked the first-instance judgment and changed the sentence to a heavier one, stating that the first-instance judgment mistakenly convicted the defendant Liu Chongwu of ordinary murder, Cao Songshou of assault, Pan Hongsheng of possession of military firearms and ammunition, and Tian Shuiyang of endangering safety. The basis for convicting the defendants was roughly as follows: "The defendants are an organized group with an entire criminal plan, with the purpose of obstructing others from exercising their rights, and using murder as a means," etc. This is indeed the essence of the original judgment's conviction. The defendants committed criminal acts due to their fervent patriotism (as stated in the rationale section of the original judgment). This is the premise of the original trial's confirmation of the case. Based on this premise, although the defendants had a group organization, their entire plan must have been nothing more than an attempt to save and protect the country. To call it an entire criminal plan is completely off-topic. Moreover, according to the defendants' confessions and the police's report, their dangerous words and intimidation of merchants selling Japanese goods has been confirmed as a common fact. The occurrence of this kind of fact must have had a common purpose. The common purpose of the defendants in this case could not be other than resisting Japan and saving the country. This is the conclusion obtained by advancing from the premise confirmed by the original trial. Therefore, it can only be said that their purpose was to resist Japan and save the country, and their means was to obstruct people from exercising their rights. The original judgment mistakenly identified this key point, leading to the conclusion that the murder was premeditated. Criminal facts should always be determined based on evidence. This is clearly stipulated in Article 282 of the Criminal Procedure Law. Interpretation Example No. 1242 of the 9th Year of the Unified Ruling states: "The evidence used to determine criminal facts must have conclusive probative force and cannot be shaken by other legitimate materials. If there are other credible materials sufficient to provide corroboration, then it can be used as a basis for an affirmative determination." This has strict regulations in law and precedent. Furthermore, the collection of evidence must be extensive, and it should not rely on only one piece of evidence. Solid physical evidence should be collected, and it should not rely solely on observational circumstantial evidence. The trial court that judges crimes must state the results of the investigation in detail and concretely, and should not only make abstract speculations. This has been repeatedly established as a precedent. Now, the original trial speculated that they had a premeditated murder based solely on the group's opening behavior. According to the above-mentioned fundamental principles of law and precedent, the content of this premeditated behavior, and where the resolution was, must be actually proven before it can be used as the basis for the judgment. However, the original judgment gained nothing and speculated out of thin air, not only contradicting its confirmed premise. This is the fundamental reason why the defendants disagree with the original judgment and appeal. As for the purpose of the defendants, it is already understood by the society. Their simple and decisive means is only to prevent the purchase and sale of enemy goods. Not only was there no premeditated murder, but there was no intention to kill from the beginning. Trying to use the following facts as a reference can further prove the credibility. (1) Before throwing the bomb, Sun Guangxing warned Xie Bintai to avoid it quickly (see Xie Bintai's confession on December 9, 21st year). This alone is sufficient to prove that there was no intention to kill. Xie Bintai and Wang Yirong have no personal grudges with the defendants. There is no reason to save one and premeditate to kill the other. (2) In the De Yuanchang case, the defendant Chongwu put the bomb in through the door seam on the floor (see the first-instance transcript), so his intention not to harm anyone is already clear. (3) The Dawangmiao meeting resolved to carry out work, that is, to warn against importing Japanese goods. As for carrying handguns, it was because the Japanese Red Shirts were harmful and had to be used for self-defense (court testimony on December 29, 21st year). According to this confession, the group meeting only intended to threaten the sale of enemy goods, and there was absolutely no intention to harm the lives of others. This is already clear as fire. (4) In the Yuyuanheng case, Wang Yirong dragged the defendant Chongwu, and the force was too strong, causing the switch to be touched and misfired (see the court testimony on January 5th of this year). This unfortunate incident was really an accidental occurrence during the journey. There was absolutely no intention to kill, let alone premeditated murder. Based on the above facts, the revised judgment of premeditated murder, although it avoids the suspicion of deliberately finding fault, should be requested by the Supreme Court to abolish the original judgment according to law and declare the appellants innocent, which is both in the public interest. Respectfully submitted to the Supreme Court.

Shanxi Discovers the Oldest Buddhist Scriptures

Shanxi Correspondence: The Shanghai Photographic Printing Song Dynasty Buddhist Scriptures Association previously sent Venerable Fancheng to visit scriptures in Shaanxi and Shanxi. More than 5,000 volumes of ancient scriptures have now been discovered in Guangshang Temple in Zhaocheng, Shanxi. They are arranged according to the Thousand Character Classic and are in the form of hand scrolls. At the end of the "Lu Character Transmission Lantern Jade Ying Scroll", there is a postscript from the second year of Jingyou of the Song Dynasty (Bingzi year of Emperor Renzong). The benefactors were mostly people from Puzhou in southern Shanxi. Examining the beginning of its printing, it should have started in the Five Dynasties. Each wooden board has 23 lines on one side, with 14 characters per line. The font is extremely simple and ancient. This kind of precious book has never been seen in domestic public or private records. Even those who collect Buddhist scriptures abroad have never seen it. In the history of Buddhist studies and editions, it is truly an unprecedented creation. Xu Junsenyu from Beiping heard the news and rushed to Guangshang Temple to borrow it. He first transported it to Beiping, and after it was publicly read by fellow Buddhists, it was transferred to Shanghai for the association to reprint.

Claims to be an inspector of the Garrison Headquarters

Discovered, arrested, and judged to be transferred

Regulations for the Management of Prostitutes in the French Concession

The Shanghai French Concession Board of Directors recently promulgated the Regulations for the Management of Prostitutes, which are recorded as follows: (Article 1) All brothels shall be subject to the following special regulations. All provisions of the Category C regulations that do not conflict with the provisions of this chapter shall be followed by all brothels. (Article 2) Brothels shall not be opened in areas that may affect neighbors. The windows of the brothel shall be covered with double gauze curtains during the day, and the blinds shall be closed at night. A bright lamp shall be hung in a conspicuous place in front of the gate and lit at sunset. (Article 3) Gambling, disputes, and immoral activities are prohibited in brothels, and the use of narcotics is prohibited. Brothels shall not be allowed to harbor people wanted by the police station or vagrants, nor shall they be allowed to reside in or accept people who depend on women's prostitution for a living, or people similar to them. If a brothel violates this article, the French Consul General may decide to close it temporarily or permanently. (Article 4) No alcohol shall be sold in the brothel or in any part of the brothel. (Article 5) Brothels are strictly prohibited from harboring or employing people under the age of 18 under any name. (Article 6) Brothels are strictly prohibited from employing or harboring women suffering from infectious diseases. (Article 7) Brothels are strictly prohibited from harboring women who are more than six months pregnant. All prostitutes should be examined by a doctor upon entering the brothel, and should be examined once a month. (Article 8) Each prostitute shall obtain a certificate card from the police station. The card shall have a photo of the prostitute and shall state some reference information about her identity (such as name, age, and place of origin), and shall state the results of the doctor's examination. The card is issued free of charge and is strictly limited to personal use. It shall not be lent, sold, or exchanged. The certificate card shall be presented immediately when requested by the police or customers. If it is lost or damaged, it may be reissued, but a fee of one yuan shall be paid, and a fine of five to twenty yuan shall be paid according to the circumstances. Brothels are strictly prohibited from harboring or accommodating women who do not have a certificate card. (Article 9) If a prostitute is found to have an infectious disease, in addition to immediately canceling the prostitute's notice and certificate card, the brothel shall also be fined. For each prostitute found to be sick, a fine of five to twenty yuan shall be imposed. If there is a repeat offense, the French Consul General may order the police station to close the brothel. (Article 10) Brothels shall report the dates of arrival and departure of the prostitutes to the police station, and shall supervise the prostitutes to comply with the provisions of this chapter.

A Group of Thugs Destroys Longyuan Teahouse

Reason... Listening to Baitanh Huang is not allowed

Result... 25 people arrested

All the electric lights in the hall were destroyed and extinguished

Teapots and teacups were thrown around in a chaotic manner

Three cars were destroyed

Two axes were confiscated

Longyuan Teahouse, located at No. 1 Houmalukou, Jiaojiaodu, Shanghai West, was suddenly attacked by twelve thugs dressed in short clothes at about 9 p.m. on the 26th of this month (i.e., last Saturday). They swarmed upstairs and went straight into the Tanh Huang performance area. The ticket seller immediately stepped forward to collect the ticket money (the standard rate is 34 copper coins per person). The thugs gave 8 cents in small money. Because the amount was not enough, the ticket seller asked them to make up the difference. The thugs were very aggressive and shouted loudly. They left their seats one after another. The ticket seller returned the 8 cents in small money to them, because they did not listen to the performance. They refused to accept it and left, saying that someone would come to get it and give you a hard time. Because of this, they wanted to retaliate. At 8:20 p.m. the night before, they gathered a large group of thugs, numbering hundreds, each holding weapons. They took nine chartered cars and two No. 16 trolleybuses and headed west from Shanghai. The cars arrived at Jiaojiaochang first and stopped. They swarmed into the teahouse and shouted loudly. The full-scale fight began immediately. First, all the electric lights in the hall were destroyed and extinguished. Then, teapots and teacups were thrown around in a chaotic manner. The order was in chaos. Fortunately, armed police and all the members of the security regiment arrived at the same time and surrounded the teahouse, and made every effort to suppress the situation to avoid injuries. Four cars, electric lights, teacups, tables and chairs were destroyed. Twenty-five thugs were arrested on the spot. The rest had fled separately. Two axes were confiscated and taken into custody. District Officer Jiang first interrogated Wu Fushun, the owner of the teahouse, and Ge Yibao, the manager, and then interrogated the thugs. They all confessed to being accomplices. Most of them were pig killers. Half of them returned halfway because they heard the alarm on the tram. After obtaining the confessions, the district officer believed that the thugs had gathered a crowd to cause trouble without any reason, carried weapons to commit violence, and disturbed the peace. They were really hateful. Yesterday, he prepared a document and sent them to the General Bureau for interrogation. The names of the thugs are recorded below: Dong Hongjun, Xu Xilin, Huang Shaofu, Sun Qilang, Pang Bojin, Sun Jingen, Yao Asan, San Wenrui, Wu Shenrui, Qiang Hongrui, Zhou Afang, Zhu Shengrong, Jin Genrui, Liu Hanzhuan, Qiu Zhengqi, Xu Zhongying, Dai Binggen, Liu Dalang, Shi Shilin, Li Amao, Pan Baolang, Xu Mingde, Cai Ronglang, Qian Rengui, Yao Shengxiang, a total of twenty-five people.

Original plan drawn by Lee Wai Pak

Fan claims that Lee assisted with the drawing

Mr. Fan Wan Chiu, a famous architect of this port, recently the Government of Kwangtung Province was planning to construct a provincial government building. At the time, Mr. Fan had asked Lee to draw the design plan, and Lee had taken on the responsibility of creating the drafts, and it took him three months to complete it. Because Lee was in Kwangtung at the time, and did not have a communications address, he gave the design to Fan. However, after Fan had received the design, he wrote a code on the plan, and used the name of Fan's Shanghai Surveying and Mapping Office and mailed it to the Kwangtung Provincial Government. Also, Fan said that Lee had assisted in the drafting of the plan. When it was announced that he was chosen for first place, Fan did not tell Mr. Lee, and went alone to Kwangtung province, but Mr. Lee found out about it soon after, and also tracked down to Kwangtung, where he is negotiating with Fan. He has also expressed his willingness to make concessions, and wished to have half of the award money, however Fan had refused, saying that the plan was submitted under the name of the surveying office, and the award should be received under the name of the office. Currently based on the report of Mr. Lee who had written a letter from Kwangtung to Shanghai, he has hired Kwangtung's lawyer Du Zhi Ding, who wrote a letter to the director of the Kwangtung Construction Bureau, Lin Wun Kai, declaring that the award money should only be given after both he and Mr. Fan had signed it. At the time, he did not have an address in Shanghai, and so they still wrote the Fan Jun Office when the plan was sent, and Wai Pak is not an employee of that office. Afterwards with Mr. Xu Jingzhi and Mr. Yang Rujun, he had formed the Xingye Architect Office at No. 19, Museum Road, Shanghai, which he had informed your office for review. Please send the information about the reward money and project progress to this address. I have also heard that the design has been ranked first place, and the award will be given in the day. The design should be listed under the names of Mr. Fan and Wai Pak together. Please inform them etc., this lawyer has confirmed that this is the truth. Hereby informing you, that in the future, to issue the award money, please order Fan Wan Zhao to come together with Lee Wai Pak to receive it, so that no argument can be made, so that the friendship is preserved, Lawyer Du Zhi Ding.

Municipal Works Bureau Implements a Method for Landowners to Fill Land in the City Center District

Since the implementation of the Greater Shanghai Plan, the Municipal Works Bureau has devoted all its efforts to the construction of the city center area. Most of the road, ditch, and bridge projects within the two land reclamation areas have been completed. The solemn and beautiful new Municipal Government Building is about to be completed, and the office buildings of various bureaus have also been completed. It is heard that the Municipal Government, in order to encourage citizens to build houses, will exempt those who build houses in the city center area from paying house donations for two years. The Municipal Works Bureau also has regulations for handling soil filling. Because after the construction of roads in the area, the land on both sides has become low-lying. It is not possible to engage in construction unless it is filled to a considerable degree. If the soil filling work is carried out by the individual owners, it will not only be difficult to obtain soil, but also the labor costs will be high, which is extremely uneconomical. Now that the bureau is planning to handle it comprehensively, it is a great convenience. The method for handling the soil filling is a total of five articles: "㈠ If the landowners want to raise the foundation, they can first submit it to the Municipal Works Bureau for registration. ㈡ The land height is determined by the Works Bureau. If it needs to be raised or lowered according to regulations, it should be declared in advance during registration. ㈢ The soil filling project is handled by the Works Bureau bidding on behalf of the owners. The landowners pay the soil price according to the bid price. ㈣ The labor cost for the required soil filling is estimated by the Works Bureau in advance and notified. The applicant pays three-quarters of the total amount in advance. This amount is collected by the Municipal Center Expense Management Committee on behalf of the applicant. After the project is completed, the contractor and the applicant inspect and accept the project, and then pay the soil price according to the actual measured amount. ㈤ If there is a dispute during the receipt of the soil, the review estimate of the Works Bureau shall be the standard, and neither party shall have any objection." Since the promulgation of this method, landowners such as the Shanghai Bank have requested that it be handled on their behalf and have been very enthusiastic.

Qian Yizhang's Funeral was Held Yesterday

The Central Government sent a representative to pay tribute

Qian Yizhang (i.e., Huang Yonghua), the Standing Committee Member of the China Seamen's Special Party Department and the Director of the Special Group of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, was extremely serious in handling his duties, which led to the jealousy of the Communists. He was assassinated at the New New Hotel at 10 p.m. on the 25th of this month. The funeral was jointly organized by the Shanghai Public Security Bureau Seamen's Special Party Department at the Public Security Bureau. The funeral was held at the Chinese Funeral Home on Haige Road at 2 p.m. yesterday. The situation is briefly recorded below:

Funeral Home Arrangement: Both the left and right gates of the Chinese Funeral Home were decorated with plain-colored arches. Many special police officers of the Public Security Bureau were armed and on guard. The hall was set up with a portrait and a blood-stained uniform, and hundreds of eulogies and couplets were hung, as well as more than 300 wreaths.
